<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c9c9a4a4dea04bdabbb67e80c744d711"><span data-offset-key="c9c9a4a4dea04bdabbb67e80c744d711:0">Other Built-in Types</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0f979c29b7224b2ea43abd97132aa25b"><span data-offset-key="0f979c29b7224b2ea43abd97132aa25b:0">The interpreter supports several other kinds of objects. Most of these support only one or two operations.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d547c3bcac654fe7b163d3e3b10dc59c"><span data-offset-key="d547c3bcac654fe7b163d3e3b10dc59c:0">Modules</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef"><span data-offset-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef:0">The only special operation on a module is attribute access: </span><span data-offset-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef:1">`m.name`</span><span data-offset-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef:2">, where </span><span data-offset-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef:3">*m*</span><span data-offset-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef:4"> is a module and </span><span data-offset-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef:5">*name*</span><span data-offset-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef:6"> accesses a name defined in </span><span data-offset-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef:7">*m*</span><span data-offset-key="2bf2171eb2d4436aab6c8f47eeac41ef:8">’s symbol table. Module attributes can be assigned to. (Note that the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4d00187895f34458a58a9c7e78beb6a6"><span data-offset-key="4d00187895f34458a58a9c7e78beb6a6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92"><span data-offset-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92:0"> statement is not, strictly speaking, an operation on a module object; </span><span data-offset-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92:1">`import foo`</span><span data-offset-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92:2"> does not require a module object named </span><span data-offset-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92:3">*foo*</span><span data-offset-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92:4"> to exist, rather it requires an (external) </span><span data-offset-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92:5">*definition*</span><span data-offset-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92:6"> for a module named </span><span data-offset-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92:7">*foo*</span><span data-offset-key="63fe32c3623e4f45a6c8fb6313c41a92:8"> somewhere.)</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fb3e4ba2626b471f936d50e2bca6b4cb"><span data-offset-key="fb3e4ba2626b471f936d50e2bca6b4cb:0">A special attribute of every module is </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#object.__dict__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6b2403b45fd642d4a0fab39ab4ffb384"><span data-offset-key="6b2403b45fd642d4a0fab39ab4ffb384:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">__dict__</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5b37da4a4e94459db364bfe516ba1c2d"><span data-offset-key="5b37da4a4e94459db364bfe516ba1c2d:0">. This is the dictionary containing the module’s symbol table. Modifying this dictionary will actually change the module’s symbol table, but direct assignment to the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#object.__dict__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d4655b9215d64555a682718022815a7e"><span data-offset-key="d4655b9215d64555a682718022815a7e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">__dict__</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a"><span data-offset-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a:0"> attribute is not possible (you can write </span><span data-offset-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a:1">`m.__dict__['a'] = 1`</span><span data-offset-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a:2">, which defines </span><span data-offset-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a:3">`m.a`</span><span data-offset-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a:4"> to be </span><span data-offset-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a:5">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a:6">, but you can’t write </span><span data-offset-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a:7">`m.__dict__ = {}`</span><span data-offset-key="4238d282669d40949e965ac0b55fcf3a:8">). Modifying </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#object.__dict__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="bd06eacbc142432b930b491875937e9f"><span data-offset-key="bd06eacbc142432b930b491875937e9f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">__dict__</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ff9f7cfefe6d46d3ab4888c7c8684765"><span data-offset-key="ff9f7cfefe6d46d3ab4888c7c8684765:0"> directly is not recommended.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a5ef3155dab74c34b31148bcc2bed2f7"><span data-offset-key="a5ef3155dab74c34b31148bcc2bed2f7:0">Modules built into the interpreter are written like this: </span><span data-offset-key="a5ef3155dab74c34b31148bcc2bed2f7:1">`<module 'sys'                                       (built-in)>`</span><span data-offset-key="a5ef3155dab74c34b31148bcc2bed2f7:2">. If loaded from a file, they are written as </span><span data-offset-key="a5ef3155dab74c34b31148bcc2bed2f7:3">`<module 'os' from                                       '/usr/local/lib/pythonX.Y/os.pyc'>`</span><span data-offset-key="a5ef3155dab74c34b31148bcc2bed2f7:4">.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ab903b6a6e1a44a8a80534fc25bc3b8a"><span data-offset-key="ab903b6a6e1a44a8a80534fc25bc3b8a:0">Classes and Class Instances</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="67def989fdc64cdbaf666c38dcb9d443"><span data-offset-key="67def989fdc64cdbaf666c38dcb9d443:0">See </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#objects" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="181df9a82a564247b8755c9273621239"><span data-offset-key="181df9a82a564247b8755c9273621239:0">Objects, values and types</span></span></a><span data-key="0ff69a6be6e34b98ad36c52ce12bb165"><span data-offset-key="0ff69a6be6e34b98ad36c52ce12bb165:0"> and </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#class" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ee6a75c699934bc5ba5a3467ef387fc3"><span data-offset-key="ee6a75c699934bc5ba5a3467ef387fc3:0">Class definitions</span></span></a><span data-key="443f479e8db04d669119c9fbbdfffa69"><span data-offset-key="443f479e8db04d669119c9fbbdfffa69:0"> for these.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="183bde0ec21849be87b0c9e6de1b8f3a"><span data-offset-key="183bde0ec21849be87b0c9e6de1b8f3a:0">Functions</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f24d1016532e4e08a9d3d3beb065c5a4"><span data-offset-key="f24d1016532e4e08a9d3d3beb065c5a4:0">Function objects are created by function definitions. The only operation on a function object is to call it: </span><span data-offset-key="f24d1016532e4e08a9d3d3beb065c5a4:1">`func(argument-list)`</span><span data-offset-key="f24d1016532e4e08a9d3d3beb065c5a4:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dabdf339393c407b8861ebc62d352cc0"><span data-offset-key="dabdf339393c407b8861ebc62d352cc0:0">There are really two flavors of function objects: built-in functions and user-defined functions. Both support the same operation (to call the function), but the implementation is different, hence the different object types.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="90a6720fceba4c048da47d16a14151c8"><span data-offset-key="90a6720fceba4c048da47d16a14151c8:0">See </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#function" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b0096029b8be4ebeb9f82dc54c655906"><span data-offset-key="b0096029b8be4ebeb9f82dc54c655906:0">Function definitions</span></span></a><span data-key="127b876bbd8246fea20c4a4aa5d34b8b"><span data-offset-key="127b876bbd8246fea20c4a4aa5d34b8b:0"> for more information.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="33a9d0c915a24d689265049f91a92b7b"><span data-offset-key="33a9d0c915a24d689265049f91a92b7b:0">Methods</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="976188b6daca4020b046910a1c5251d8"><span data-offset-key="976188b6daca4020b046910a1c5251d8:0">Methods are functions that are called using the attribute notation. There are two flavors: built-in methods (such as </span><span data-offset-key="976188b6daca4020b046910a1c5251d8:1">`append()`</span><span data-offset-key="976188b6daca4020b046910a1c5251d8:2"> on lists) and class instance methods. Built-in methods are described with the types that support them.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84"><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:0">If you access a method (a function defined in a class namespace) through an instance, you get a special object: a </span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:1">*bound method*</span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:2"> (also called </span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:3">*instance method*</span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:4">) object. When called, it will add the </span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:5">`self`</span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:6"> argument to the argument list. Bound methods have two special read-only attributes: </span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:7">`m.__self__`</span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:8"> is the object on which the method operates, and </span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:9">`m.__func__`</span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:10"> is the function implementing the method. Calling </span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:11">`m(arg-1, arg-2, ..., arg-n)`</span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:12"> is completely equivalent to calling </span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:13">`m.__func__(m.__self__, arg-1, arg-2, ...,                                       arg-n)`</span><span data-offset-key="0583032907ef422d9f9d68f7c1862b84:14">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fd1e572c74e3494087cc9442da90715b"><span data-offset-key="fd1e572c74e3494087cc9442da90715b:0">Like function objects, bound method objects support getting arbitrary attributes. However, since method attributes are actually stored on the underlying function object (</span><span data-offset-key="fd1e572c74e3494087cc9442da90715b:1">`meth.__func__`</span><span data-offset-key="fd1e572c74e3494087cc9442da90715b:2">), setting method attributes on bound methods is disallowed. Attempting to set an attribute on a method results in an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#AttributeError" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fe9aa278761a45b795bd442224e9e263"><span data-offset-key="fe9aa278761a45b795bd442224e9e263:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">AttributeError</code></span></span></a><span data-key="fb5b1c886fa148c2a137100aaa569f4e"><span data-offset-key="fb5b1c886fa148c2a137100aaa569f4e:0"> being raised. In order to set a method attribute, you need to explicitly set it on the underlying function object:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> class C:...     def method(self):...         pass...>>> c = C()>>> c.method.whoami = 'my name is method'  # can't set on the methodTraceback (most recent call last):  File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>AttributeError: 'method' object has no attribute 'whoami'>>> c.method.__func__.whoami = 'my name is method'>>> c.method.whoami'my name is method'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5cebf326c18b4c87a8b9dbcf11d4ce50"><span data-offset-key="5cebf326c18b4c87a8b9dbcf11d4ce50:0">See </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#types" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6aed3a5b25f84c3fa7273e717e206249"><span data-offset-key="6aed3a5b25f84c3fa7273e717e206249:0">The standard type hierarchy</span></span></a><span data-key="e225c17b76b74c118dd1a8e9510e2d0a"><span data-offset-key="e225c17b76b74c118dd1a8e9510e2d0a:0"> for more information.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="beecb9fedcd544bf99e0116d88e5882d"><span data-offset-key="beecb9fedcd544bf99e0116d88e5882d:0">Code Objects</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cdc802e714df47868812cb79179af4d8"><span data-offset-key="cdc802e714df47868812cb79179af4d8:0">Code objects are used by the implementation to represent “pseudo-compiled” executable Python code such as a function body. They differ from function objects because they don’t contain a reference to their global execution environment. Code objects are returned by the built-in </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#compile" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b9e5711b5d944e6fad29f6acbf39f3a7"><span data-offset-key="b9e5711b5d944e6fad29f6acbf39f3a7:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">compile()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ca09bf5f493747c58986e99b84a66142"><span data-offset-key="ca09bf5f493747c58986e99b84a66142:0"> function and can be extracted from function objects through their </span><span data-offset-key="ca09bf5f493747c58986e99b84a66142:1">`__code__`</span><span data-offset-key="ca09bf5f493747c58986e99b84a66142:2"> attribute. See also the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/code.html#module-code" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="99ece5473a5843c0979e828f30119e1e"><span data-offset-key="99ece5473a5843c0979e828f30119e1e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">code</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e22f92c84f3c4084a714c9c5bae81806"><span data-offset-key="e22f92c84f3c4084a714c9c5bae81806:0"> module.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7b08e438a012440fb85738dc96e56dec"><span data-offset-key="7b08e438a012440fb85738dc96e56dec:0">Accessing </span><span data-offset-key="7b08e438a012440fb85738dc96e56dec:1">`__code__`</span><span data-offset-key="7b08e438a012440fb85738dc96e56dec:2"> raises an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#auditing" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2704400356ed4d8e91ee3c21a83992e8"><span data-offset-key="2704400356ed4d8e91ee3c21a83992e8:0">auditing event</span></span></a><span data-key="b3849147afbd4456b3479cd0d27ee701"><span data-offset-key="b3849147afbd4456b3479cd0d27ee701:0"> </span><span data-offset-key="b3849147afbd4456b3479cd0d27ee701:1">`object.__getattr__`</span><span data-offset-key="b3849147afbd4456b3479cd0d27ee701:2"> with arguments </span><span data-offset-key="b3849147afbd4456b3479cd0d27ee701:3">`obj`</span><span data-offset-key="b3849147afbd4456b3479cd0d27ee701:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="b3849147afbd4456b3479cd0d27ee701:5">`"__code__"`</span><span data-offset-key="b3849147afbd4456b3479cd0d27ee701:6">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9142e6d9903d438aabd058a1348ba2ae"><span data-offset-key="9142e6d9903d438aabd058a1348ba2ae:0">A code object can be executed or evaluated by passing it (instead of a source string) to the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#exec" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5d7dcb43a1504da893251dc4ffdbb01d"><span data-offset-key="5d7dcb43a1504da893251dc4ffdbb01d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">exec()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4a64b38272864691968f05ec4e890a39"><span data-offset-key="4a64b38272864691968f05ec4e890a39:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#eval" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3429379229524320b5fdf3c4a4f0bf65"><span data-offset-key="3429379229524320b5fdf3c4a4f0bf65:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">eval()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="af2f636f85b24d9c91b1c45706e9fe66"><span data-offset-key="af2f636f85b24d9c91b1c45706e9fe66:0"> built-in functions.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e6ed8553f2374c8584f52abc6fdec95c"><span data-offset-key="e6ed8553f2374c8584f52abc6fdec95c:0">See </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#types" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="24a358fe540641528e7a566f349f9c38"><span data-offset-key="24a358fe540641528e7a566f349f9c38:0">The standard type hierarchy</span></span></a><span data-key="8a2bfa30939b4d22a6e3efca67c75912"><span data-offset-key="8a2bfa30939b4d22a6e3efca67c75912:0"> for more information.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="89371e3eca014024b93d3da14106c2c1"><span data-offset-key="89371e3eca014024b93d3da14106c2c1:0">Type Objects</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3c13f0e4123e4b6288b7be7aa0c9ce75"><span data-offset-key="3c13f0e4123e4b6288b7be7aa0c9ce75:0">Type objects represent the various object types. An object’s type is accessed by the built-in function </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#type" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2275d7d3ea0a4c2aa9aa6708aeea89cd"><span data-offset-key="2275d7d3ea0a4c2aa9aa6708aeea89cd:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">type()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="09a624b488a1452b95cb37ba6eaaee58"><span data-offset-key="09a624b488a1452b95cb37ba6eaaee58:0">. There are no special operations on types. The standard module </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/types.html#module-types" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="50c4dea4b0c242959be408b99ff06de4"><span data-offset-key="50c4dea4b0c242959be408b99ff06de4:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">types</code></span></span></a><span data-key="fb76406b947c4031a8e6b520395a7acc"><span data-offset-key="fb76406b947c4031a8e6b520395a7acc:0"> defines names for all standard built-in types.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0999a745b807430e8739b87053dcb955"><span data-offset-key="0999a745b807430e8739b87053dcb955:0">Types are written like this: </span><span data-offset-key="0999a745b807430e8739b87053dcb955:1">`<class 'int'>`</span><span data-offset-key="0999a745b807430e8739b87053dcb955:2">.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a83e2e1867314dfda6b06c4c62f3dfeb"><span data-offset-key="a83e2e1867314dfda6b06c4c62f3dfeb:0">The Null Object</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f3eaee15e023464bb134e3e8e2a8158c"><span data-offset-key="f3eaee15e023464bb134e3e8e2a8158c:0">This object is returned by functions that don’t explicitly return a value. It supports no special operations. There is exactly one null object, named </span><span data-offset-key="f3eaee15e023464bb134e3e8e2a8158c:1">`None`</span><span data-offset-key="f3eaee15e023464bb134e3e8e2a8158c:2"> (a built-in name). </span><span data-offset-key="f3eaee15e023464bb134e3e8e2a8158c:3">`type(None)()`</span><span data-offset-key="f3eaee15e023464bb134e3e8e2a8158c:4"> produces the same singleton.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5264eb3e575b437f8e6a91d2e780e531"><span data-offset-key="5264eb3e575b437f8e6a91d2e780e531:0">It is written as </span><span data-offset-key="5264eb3e575b437f8e6a91d2e780e531:1">`None`</span><span data-offset-key="5264eb3e575b437f8e6a91d2e780e531:2">.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0c72a04c05e24c86a94f371e9e9dfba6"><span data-offset-key="0c72a04c05e24c86a94f371e9e9dfba6:0">The Ellipsis Object</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6fd7da70691449e3801f8545348849a9"><span data-offset-key="6fd7da70691449e3801f8545348849a9:0">This object is commonly used by slicing (see </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/expressions.html#slicings" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e279f8b7b3e9490883cc3372865bb4e7"><span data-offset-key="e279f8b7b3e9490883cc3372865bb4e7:0">Slicings</span></span></a><span data-key="49cc68ac4aad426ea8f445b20e69d7fb"><span data-offset-key="49cc68ac4aad426ea8f445b20e69d7fb:0">). It supports no special operations. There is exactly one ellipsis object, named </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#Ellipsis" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f7cb45f6bcd44cc1bca849c02319eee9"><span data-offset-key="f7cb45f6bcd44cc1bca849c02319eee9:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">Ellipsis</code></span></span></a><span data-key="22c0610410fc4c66b869ba493ee259ec"><span data-offset-key="22c0610410fc4c66b869ba493ee259ec:0"> (a built-in name). </span><span data-offset-key="22c0610410fc4c66b869ba493ee259ec:1">`type(Ellipsis)()`</span><span data-offset-key="22c0610410fc4c66b869ba493ee259ec:2"> produces the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#Ellipsis" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3b5b4d17561a49b29aef7ac97d985633"><span data-offset-key="3b5b4d17561a49b29aef7ac97d985633:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">Ellipsis</code></span></span></a><span data-key="adf80bfad3a64e42b174c6d00a65a64e"><span data-offset-key="adf80bfad3a64e42b174c6d00a65a64e:0"> singleton.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0d3354edf6fd4e2995225debfb2f8955"><span data-offset-key="0d3354edf6fd4e2995225debfb2f8955:0">It is written as </span><span data-offset-key="0d3354edf6fd4e2995225debfb2f8955:1">`Ellipsis`</span><span data-offset-key="0d3354edf6fd4e2995225debfb2f8955:2"> or </span><span data-offset-key="0d3354edf6fd4e2995225debfb2f8955:3">`...`</span><span data-offset-key="0d3354edf6fd4e2995225debfb2f8955:4">.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="76c18bb21ceb493390d98fa632536746"><span data-offset-key="76c18bb21ceb493390d98fa632536746:0">The NotImplemented Object</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="732f9639cb6e4d229c06f50823d411c4"><span data-offset-key="732f9639cb6e4d229c06f50823d411c4:0">This object is returned from comparisons and binary operations when they are asked to operate on types they don’t support. See </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/expressions.html#comparisons" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1c086107cc8a4a84bed5e13456197e5c"><span data-offset-key="1c086107cc8a4a84bed5e13456197e5c:0">Comparisons</span></span></a><span data-key="676232d184fe4f8d881fd8b93bcf6de7"><span data-offset-key="676232d184fe4f8d881fd8b93bcf6de7:0"> for more information. There is exactly one </span><span data-offset-key="676232d184fe4f8d881fd8b93bcf6de7:1">`NotImplemented`</span><span data-offset-key="676232d184fe4f8d881fd8b93bcf6de7:2"> object. </span><span data-offset-key="676232d184fe4f8d881fd8b93bcf6de7:3">`type(NotImplemented)()`</span><span data-offset-key="676232d184fe4f8d881fd8b93bcf6de7:4"> produces the singleton instance.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9700f93111964ce5aead3dfe39ee34be"><span data-offset-key="9700f93111964ce5aead3dfe39ee34be:0">It is written as </span><span data-offset-key="9700f93111964ce5aead3dfe39ee34be:1">`NotImplemented`</span><span data-offset-key="9700f93111964ce5aead3dfe39ee34be:2">.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6fac4078a7fe4250b9a62862bd434432"><span data-offset-key="6fac4078a7fe4250b9a62862bd434432:0">Boolean Values</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2ba4f97b071b447cb90e4b4690faa8b8"><span data-offset-key="2ba4f97b071b447cb90e4b4690faa8b8:0">Boolean values are the two constant objects </span><span data-offset-key="2ba4f97b071b447cb90e4b4690faa8b8:1">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="2ba4f97b071b447cb90e4b4690faa8b8:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="2ba4f97b071b447cb90e4b4690faa8b8:3">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="2ba4f97b071b447cb90e4b4690faa8b8:4">. They are used to represent truth values (although other values can also be considered false or true). In numeric contexts (for example when used as the argument to an arithmetic operator), they behave like the integers 0 and 1, respectively. The built-in function </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4c1839708e594fa9a3f95d3b7d132152"><span data-offset-key="4c1839708e594fa9a3f95d3b7d132152:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">bool()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c5614b2c7d8d4a24a51bcc857716e239"><span data-offset-key="c5614b2c7d8d4a24a51bcc857716e239:0"> can be used to convert any value to a Boolean, if the value can be interpreted as a truth value (see section </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#truth" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="de5d46cb398a4dd193f2e8cf36a62260"><span data-offset-key="de5d46cb398a4dd193f2e8cf36a62260:0">Truth Value Testing</span></span></a><span data-key="c753b43fddfc4eaf847cfcba7655c0a9"><span data-offset-key="c753b43fddfc4eaf847cfcba7655c0a9:0"> above).</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f82d99d097934fa88cac4404c6a2f34a"><span data-offset-key="f82d99d097934fa88cac4404c6a2f34a:0">They are written as </span><span data-offset-key="f82d99d097934fa88cac4404c6a2f34a:1">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="f82d99d097934fa88cac4404c6a2f34a:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="f82d99d097934fa88cac4404c6a2f34a:3">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="f82d99d097934fa88cac4404c6a2f34a:4">, respectively.</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="69f3b518ee9947aea022f42fa1995b07"><span data-offset-key="69f3b518ee9947aea022f42fa1995b07:0">Internal Objects</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e29150e9b93640029a0439dd64400879"><span data-offset-key="e29150e9b93640029a0439dd64400879:0">See </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#types" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="11a1d8eb00bf4c64bc09c4da599e98ba"><span data-offset-key="11a1d8eb00bf4c64bc09c4da599e98ba:0">The standard type hierarchy</span></span></a><span data-key="9095e0b76dc64099bef9252236ab4973"><span data-offset-key="9095e0b76dc64099bef9252236ab4973:0"> for this information. It describes stack frame objects, traceback objects, and slice objects.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="17e34e776e5c4ca7b67722dddd97a6f7"><span data-offset-key="17e34e776e5c4ca7b67722dddd97a6f7:0">Special Attributes</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b53ac9034a2a4c54ad440bc72c9fa31a"><span data-offset-key="b53ac9034a2a4c54ad440bc72c9fa31a:0">The implementation adds a few special read-only attributes to several object types, where they are relevant. Some of these are not reported by the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#dir" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="acd7ee3057fb4346914219bbe20bfa82"><span data-offset-key="acd7ee3057fb4346914219bbe20bfa82:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">dir()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="bfe26322bb6344ea8516b0942cb721dc"><span data-offset-key="bfe26322bb6344ea8516b0942cb721dc:0"> built-in function.</span><span data-offset-key="bfe26322bb6344ea8516b0942cb721dc:1">`object.__dict__`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="82dded9bafed4ba290d7b96d915182d0"><span data-offset-key="82dded9bafed4ba290d7b96d915182d0:0">A dictionary or other mapping object used to store an object’s (writable) attributes.</span><span data-offset-key="82dded9bafed4ba290d7b96d915182d0:1">`instance.__class__`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8819d9ad254a420ebbf676d0f0a7a72e"><span data-offset-key="8819d9ad254a420ebbf676d0f0a7a72e:0">The class to which a class instance belongs.</span><span data-offset-key="8819d9ad254a420ebbf676d0f0a7a72e:1">`class.__bases__`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b1c4067716424d4cb4ce8e5cd7ee1c98"><span data-offset-key="b1c4067716424d4cb4ce8e5cd7ee1c98:0">The tuple of base classes of a class object.</span><span data-offset-key="b1c4067716424d4cb4ce8e5cd7ee1c98:1">`definition.__name__`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dad1683c7ba142a1baac03cc8f38ee80"><span data-offset-key="dad1683c7ba142a1baac03cc8f38ee80:0">The name of the class, function, method, descriptor, or generator instance.</span><span data-offset-key="dad1683c7ba142a1baac03cc8f38ee80:1">`definition.__qualname__`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7352540594bb44ce834ee63127ddbda1"><span data-offset-key="7352540594bb44ce834ee63127ddbda1:0">The </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-qualified-name" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ff3f449f72f94b6682e9dd474799a9f8"><span data-offset-key="ff3f449f72f94b6682e9dd474799a9f8:0">qualified name</span></span></a><span data-key="8db4fe70c3384274a38db69af47ad05e"><span data-offset-key="8db4fe70c3384274a38db69af47ad05e:0"> of the class, function, method, descriptor, or generator instance.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8fd36d28c49f4918a08f8cb9aae58cd9"><span data-offset-key="8fd36d28c49f4918a08f8cb9aae58cd9:0">New in version 3.3.</span><span data-offset-key="8fd36d28c49f4918a08f8cb9aae58cd9:1">`class.__mro__`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4bed1ef4c381415eb95618adacc41f39"><span data-offset-key="4bed1ef4c381415eb95618adacc41f39:0">This attribute is a tuple of classes that are considered when looking for base classes during method resolution.</span><span data-offset-key="4bed1ef4c381415eb95618adacc41f39:1">`class.mro`</span><span data-offset-key="4bed1ef4c381415eb95618adacc41f39:2">()</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c19e1c0012e24cef83a9f9ddee39155a"><span data-offset-key="c19e1c0012e24cef83a9f9ddee39155a:0">This method can be overridden by a metaclass to customize the method resolution order for its instances. It is called at class instantiation, and its result is stored in </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#class.__mro__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b6e4d9ede5524089b7338dda3442ac6d"><span data-offset-key="b6e4d9ede5524089b7338dda3442ac6d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">__mro__</code></span></span></a><span data-key="61ded7ffd18444f0963171411ebd57b6"><span data-offset-key="61ded7ffd18444f0963171411ebd57b6:0">.</span><span data-offset-key="61ded7ffd18444f0963171411ebd57b6:1">`class.__subclasses__`</span><span data-offset-key="61ded7ffd18444f0963171411ebd57b6:2">()</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="21a4ac973c494ba4a90a055566df2847"><span data-offset-key="21a4ac973c494ba4a90a055566df2847:0">Each class keeps a list of weak references to its immediate subclasses. This method returns a list of all those references still alive. The list is in definition order. Example:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> int.__subclasses__()[<class 'bool'>]

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1">Built-in Types</span></span>

<a href="untitled-2.html#truth-value-testing" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Truth Value Testing</span></span>

<a href="untitled-2.html#boolean-operations-and-or-not" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Boolean Operations — and, or, not</span></span>

<a href="untitled-2.html#comparisons" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Comparisons</span></span>

<a href="untitled-2.html#numeric-types-int-float-complex" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Numeric Types — int, float, complex</span></span>

<a href="untitled-2.html#iterator-types" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>
